Two Deviant Extremes: Blind Imitation and Overreliance on Reason
Ghazali criticizes the Hashwiyya for excessive literalism and the philosophers/extreme Mu'tazila for overreliance on reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's critique of two groups: the Hashwiyya who neglect reason and the philosophers/Mu'tazila who overstep its bounds.

Core Idea
Both neglecting reason and overusing it are deviations from the middle path.

After praising the balanced approach of Ahl al-Sunnah, al-Ghazali turns to criticize two groups that have fallen into error: the Hashwiyya, who blindly cling to tradition without using reason, and the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila, who overextend reason to the point of contradicting definitive religious texts. Both extremes are condemned as stemming from weak intellects or corrupted consciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the criticism of the Hashwiyya
Notice that Ghazali says they thought it obligatory to freeze on blind imitation (الجمود على التقليد) and follow negligence (التفريط).
This shows their error is from weak intellects and lack of insight.
2
Read the criticism of the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila
They delved too much into the exercise of reason until they clashed with categorical proofs of the law.
Ghazali attributes their error to corrupted consciences (الضمائر).
3
Compare the two errors
One is negligence (tafrīṭ), the other is excess (ifrāṭ). Both are far from firmness (حزم) and caution (احتياط).
This sets up the need for a middle path.

?

The Obligation of the Middle Path (Iqtisād)
Ghazali prescribes the middle path as the mandatory way in belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's conclusion that the only correct course in matters of belief is the middle path between negligence and excess.

Core Idea
The straight path is the middle path, avoiding both extremes.

Having identified the two deviant extremes, al-Ghazali now states the positive duty: to adhere to the middle path (iqtisād) and proceed on the straight path (ṣirāṭ mustaqīm). He quotes a famous poetic line to reinforce that both extremes are blameworthy and the middle is praiseworthy. This sets the methodological foundation for his entire book: a balanced approach that avoids the errors of both excessive literalism and excessive rationalism.

Guided Path
1
Read the imperative statement
Notice the phrase 'الواجب المحتوم' — the necessary and obligatory — indicating that following the middle path is not optional.
This is a strong claim.
2
Understand the term Iqtisād
Iqtisād means moderation, the middle way. It is contrasted with tafrīṭ and ifrāṭ.
The title of the book, 'al-Iqtisād fī al-I'tiqād', reflects this focus.
3
Reflect on the poetic line
The line says both extremes are blameworthy and the middle matters lead to success.
This is a common wisdom in Islamic ethics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وبِه نَسْتَعِينُ
قال الشيخ الإمامُ، حجَّةُ الإسلام، أبو حامد محمد بن محمد بن محمد الغزالي قدَّسَ الله روحه:
الحمدُ لله الذي اجتبى من صفوة عباده عِصابة الحقِّ وأهل السنة، وخصهم من بين سائر الفرق بمزايا اللطف والمنة، وأفاض عليهم من نور هدايته ما كشَفَ لهم به عن حقائق الدين، وأنطق ألسنتهم بحجَّتِهِ التي قمع بها ضَلالَ الملحدين، وصفّى سرائرهم عن وساوس الشياطين، وطهَّرَ ضمائرهم عن نزغات الزائغين، وعمَّرَ أفئدتهم بأنوار اليقين؛ حتى اهتدوا بها إلى أسرار ما أنزلَهُ على لسان نبيِّهِ وصفيه محمد سيد المرسلين، صلى الله عليه وعلى آله أجمعين، فاطَّلعوا على طريق التلفيق بين مقتضيات الشرائع وموجبات العقول، وتحققوا أن لا معاندة بين الشرع المنقول والحق لمعقول، وعرفوا أنَّ من ظنَّ من الحشوية وجوب الجمود على التقليد واتباع التفريط [؟] وإفراط الفلاسفة [؟] ما أتوا إلا من ضعفِ العقول وقلَّةِ البصائر، وأنَّ من تغلغل من الفلاسفة وغُلاة المعتزلة في تصرُّف العقل حتى صادموا به قواطع الشرع، ما أتوا إلا من حيث الضمائر. فميلُ أولئك إلى التفريط، وميل هؤلاء إلى الإفراط، وكلاهما بعيدان عن الحزم والاحتياط، بل الواجب المحتوم في قواعد الاعتقاد ملازمة [الخلج؟] للاقتصاد والاستداد على الصراط المستقيم، فكلا طرفي قصدِ الأمور ذميم. وعليك بأوساط الأمور فإنها طريق إلى نجح الصواب قويم.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. And with Him we seek help. The Shaykh al-Imam, Proof of Islam, Abu Hamid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify his soul, said: Praise be to Allah who selected from the elite of His servants the party of truth and the people of the Sunnah, and singled them out from among all other sects with favors of kindness and grace, and poured upon them from the light of His guidance that which uncovered for them the realities of the religion, and made their tongues speak with His proof by which He suppressed the misguidance of the atheists, and purified their innermost beings from the whisperings of the devils, and cleansed their consciences from the incitements of the deviators, and filled their hearts with the lights of certainty; until they were guided thereby to the secrets of what He revealed upon the tongue of His Prophet and chosen one, Muhammad the master of the messengers, may Allah bless him and his family altogether. So they became acquainted with the way of reconciliation between the requirements of the revealed laws and the dictates of the intellects, and they realized that there is no opposition between the transmitted law and the intellectual truth. And they knew that those among the Hashwiyya who thought that it is obligatory to freeze on blind imitation and to follow [negligence?] and the excess of the philosophers [??] – they only came from weakness of intellects and lack of insight. And that those among the philosophers and the extreme Mu'tazila who delved into the exercise of the intellect until they clashed with the categorical proofs of the law – they only came from [corruption of] consciences. So the inclination of the first group is toward negligence, and the inclination of these is toward excess, and both are far from firmness and caution. Rather, the necessary and obligatory in the principles of belief is to adhere to the middle path and to proceed on the straight path. For both extremes of the intended matters are blameworthy. And upon you (is to adopt) the middle matters, for it is a straight path to success and correctness.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is the preface (خطبة الكتاب) of al-Ghazali's work. It begins with the basmalah and praise of Allah, then identifies the author. Al-Ghazali praises the 'party of truth and the people of the Sunnah' (Ahl al-Sunnah) as those whom Allah specially guided to reconcile the demands of revelation (sharā'i') and the dictates of reason ('uqūl). He states that they realized there is no conflict between transmitted law (shar' manqūl) and intellectual truth (haqq ma'qūl). He then criticizes two deviant groups: (1) the Hashwiyya, who blindly cling to tradition and neglect reason—their error stems from weak intellects and lack of insight; (2) the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila, who over-rely on reason and contradict definitive religious proofs—their error stems from corrupted consciences. Al-Ghazali says the first group is guilty of negligence (tafrīṭ) and the second of excess (ifrāṭ); both are far from correctness. The mandatory course in matters of belief is to adhere to the middle path (iqtisād) and to proceed on the straight path. He quotes a famous poetic line: 'Both extremes of intended matters are blameworthy, and upon you is (to adopt) the middle matters, for it is a straight path to success and correctness.' This sets the methodological foundation for his entire book: a balanced approach between reason and revelation.

Key Terms
الاقتصاد
الصراط المستقيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The middle path is just a compromise without clear basis.
Correction: Ghazali presents it as the divinely mandated straight path, not mere compromise.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say about both extremes?
A) Both are praiseworthy
B) Both are blameworthy
C) One is good, one is bad
D) Neither matters

Key Takeaway
The middle path (iqtisād) is the mandatory and successful way in Islamic belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is your faith journey marked by extremes—going overboard in one direction or falling short in another? What would it look like to consciously choose the middle path in how you practice your beliefs this week?
?
Al-Ghazali commands you to take the middle path as an obligation. Are you willing to abandon any extreme opinion or practice you hold, even if it feels comfortable, to walk the straight path that leads to success?
?
You claim to follow the straight path, but where in your life do you secretly lean toward excess or negligence—perhaps in your views on God's attributes or your daily acts of worship? What is one concrete change you will make today to restore balance?

The Balanced Path: Synthesizing Reason and Revelation
Ghazali praises Sunnis and critiques two extremes, calling for the middle path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali considers the middle path between blind traditionalism and excessive rationalism to be the only valid approach to Islamic theology.

Core Idea
True guidance requires combining reason and revelation, not choosing one over the other.

In this opening passage, Ghazali sets the stage for his entire theological work. He praises the Sunnis for their balanced approach and sharply critiques two extreme groups: the Hashwiyya who reject reason, and the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila who over-rely on it. This lesson examines why Ghazali condemns both extremes and calls for a synthesis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups Ghazali critiques
Read the passage carefully and note the characteristics of the Hashwiyya and the philosophers/Mu'tazila. What does Ghazali say about their shortcomings?
Ghazali mentions both weakness of intellect and lack of insight.
2
Understand the praised group
Notice how Ghazali describes the people of the Sunnah: they are distinguished by divine grace, given insight into combining the demands of law and reason, and freed from doubts.
3
Grasp the call for the middle path
Ghazali explicitly states that the necessary obligation is to adhere to the middle way (الاقتصاد). Reflect on why he calls both extremes blameworthy.
The phrase 'both ends are blameworthy' is a key takeaway.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وبه نستعين

قال الشيخ الإمام حجة الإسلام أبو حامد محمد بن محمد بن محمد الغزالي قدس الله روحه:

الحمد لله الذي اجتبى من صفوة عباده عصابة الحق وأهل السنة، وخصهم من بين سائر الفرق بمزايا اللطف والمنة، وأفاض عليهم من نور هدايته ما كشف لهم به عن حقائق الدين، وأنطق ألسنتهم بحجته التي قمع بها ضلال الملحدين، وصفى سرائرهم عن وساوس الشياطين، وطهر ضمائرهم عن نزغات الزائغين، وعمر أفئدتهم بأنوار اليقين؛ حتى اهتدوا بها إلى أسرار ما أنزله على لسان نبيه وصفيه محمد سيد المرسلين، صلى الله عليه وعلى آله أجمعين، فاطلعوا على طريق التلفيق بين مقتضيات الشرائع وموجبات العقول، وتحققوا أن لا معاندة بين الشرع المنقول والعقل المعقول، وعرفوا أن من ظن من الحشوية وجوب الجمود على التقليد واتباع التفريط الحشوية وإفراط الفلاسفة نظواهر ما أتوا إلا من ضعف العقول وقلة البصائر، وأن من تغلغل من الفلاسفة وغلاة المعتزلة في تصرف العقل حتى صادموا به قواطع الشرع أنوا إلا من حيث الضمائر.

فميل أولئك إلى التفريط، وميل هؤلاء إلى الإفراط، وكلاهما بعيد المناصير عن الحزم والاحتياط، بل الواجب المحتوم في قواعد الاعتقاد ملازمة الخلج للاقتصاد والاستداد على الصراط المستقيم، فكلا طرفي قصد الأمور دهيم.

ضرورة تلازم العقل وأنى يستتب الرشاد لمن يقنع بتقليد الأثر والخبر، وينكر مناهج البحث والنظر عند أهل النظر والنظر؟ أولا يعلم أنه لا مستند للشرع إلا قول سيد البشر، وبرهان العقل هو الذي عرف صدقه فيما أخبر؟

وكيف يهتدي للصواب من اقتفى محض العقل واقتصر، وما استضاء بنور الشرع ولا استبصر؟

فليت شعري؛ كيف يفزع إلى العقل حيث يعتريه العي والحصر؟ أولا يعلم أن خطا العقل قاصرة، وأن مجاله ضيق منحصر؟

هيهات هيهات قد خاب على القطع والبتات، وتعثر بأذيال الضلالات من لم يجمع بتأليف العقل والشرع هذا الشتات

فمثال العقل البصر السليم عن الآفات والأدواء، ومثال القرآن الشمس المنتشرة الضياء، فأخلق بأن يكون طالب الاهتداء، المستغني بأحدهما عن الآخر في غمار الأغبياء؛ فالمعرض عن العقل اكتفاء بالقرآن كالمتعرض لنور الشمس مغمضا لأجفان، فلا فرق بينه وبين العميان؛

فالعقل مع الشرع نور على نور، والملاحظ بالعين العوراء لأحدهما على الخصوص متدل بحبل غرور

أهل السنة هم وسيتضح لك أيها المتشوف إلى الاطلاع على قواعد عقائد أهل السنة، الموفقون للجمع المقترح تحقيقها بقواطع الأدلة: أنه لم يستأثر بالتوفيق للجمع بين الشرع بينهما
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, and by Him we seek help.

The Shaykh, the Imam, the Proof of Islam, Abu Hamid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify his soul, said:

Praise be to Allah who chose from the elite of His servants the party of truth and the people of the Sunnah, and distinguished them among all sects with the merits of kindness and grace, and poured upon them from the light of His guidance that by which He uncovered for them the realities of religion, and made their tongues speak with His proof by which He suppressed the misguidance of the atheists, and purified their consciences from the whisperings of devils, and cleansed their hearts from the insinuations of the deviators, and filled their hearts with the lights of certainty; until they were guided thereby to the secrets of what He revealed upon the tongue of His Prophet and chosen one, Muhammad, the master of the messengers, may Allah bless him and all his family. So they came to know the way of reconciling between the requirements of the laws and the demands of the intellects, and they realized that there is no contradiction between transmitted revelation and rational truth. And they knew that those among the Hashwiyya who thought that it is obligatory to rigidly adhere to tradition and follow [their] exaggeration—they have only come from weakness of intellects and lack of insights. And that those among the philosophers and the extremists of the Mu'tazila who delved deeply into the use of reason until they collided with the decisive proofs of the Sharia—they have only come from [deficiency of] insights.

So the inclination of the former is towards negligence, and the inclination of the latter is towards excess, and both are far from caution and prudence. Rather, the necessary obligation in the foundations of belief is to adhere to the middle way and to be steadfast on the straight path, for either extreme of affairs is blameworthy.

The necessity of the interdependence of reason—and how can right guidance be established for one who is content with blindly following transmitted tradition and denies the methods of investigation and reflection according to the people of consideration and insight? Does he not know that there is no basis for the Sharia except the speech of the master of mankind, and rational proof is what affirmed his truthfulness in what he reported?

And how can one be guided to correctness who follows pure reason exclusively, and does not seek illumination from the light of the Sharia nor gain insight?

Would that I knew; how can one resort to reason when it is afflicted by incapacity and confusion? Does he not know that the steps of reason are limited, and its field is narrow and restricted?

Far, far from it! He has certainly failed, with utter loss and ruin, and stumbled in the skirts of misguidance, whoever does not combine reason and revelation to unite this dispersion.

So the example of reason is the sound eye free from defects and diseases, and the example of the Qur'an is the sun spreading light. So how fitting it is for the seeker of guidance who dispenses with one of them in favor of the other to be among the foolish. For one who turns away from reason, contenting himself with the Qur'an, is like one who exposes himself to the sunlight with closed eyelids—there is no difference between him and the blind.

Thus reason along with revelation is light upon light, and whoever observes only one of them with a one-eyed vision clings to a rope of delusion.

The people of the Sunnah—and it will become clear to you, O aspirant to learn the foundations of the beliefs of the people of the Sunnah—are those who are granted success in combining them, as it is sought to be verified by decisive proofs: that no one is singled out for success in combining between them.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of Ghazali's introduction (خطبة الكتاب) to his work on Islamic doctrine. He first praises Allah for selecting the group of truth and the Sunnah (Ahl al-Sunna) and endowing them with the ability to reconcile the demands of divine law and rational thought. Ghazali asserts that there is no real contradiction between transmitted revelation and rational truth. He then critiques two extreme groups: the Hashwiyya, who rigidly cling to tradition and reject reason, and the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila, who over-rely on reason to the point of opposing definitive revealed texts. Both groups are blamed for lacking insight. He calls for the middle path (الاقتصاد) and steadfastness on the straight path. He provides three rhetorical questions to demonstrate that reason is necessary to verify the truthfulness of the Prophet, that pure reason without revelation is insufficient, and that reason alone has limits. He uses vivid analogies: reason is like a sound eye, the Qur'an like the sun; one who relies solely on the Qur'an without reason is like a person closing his eyes to the sun, and one who relies solely on reason without revelation is like a one-eyed observer holding a rope of delusion. The passage concludes by stating that the people of the Sunnah are the ones who successfully combine both sources.

Key Terms
عقل
شرع
حشوية
فلاسفة
معتزلة
أهل السنة
تقليد
اقتصاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ghazali is rejecting either reason or revelation entirely.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly argues that both extremes are wrong and that the truth lies in combining both reason and revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali in this passage, what is the main cause of deviation among both the Hashwiyya and the philosophers/extreme Mu'tazila?
A) They rely too much on reason.
B) They rely too much on tradition.
C) They lack insight and fail to properly combine reason and revelation.
D) They follow the wrong scholars.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali establishes that true guidance requires synthesizing reason and revelation, avoiding both blind traditionalism and excessive rationalism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you tend to lean toward blind imitation of tradition (taqlid) or toward trusting your own reasoning even when it contradicts clear revelation? Where does Ghazali's call for balance expose your imbalance, and what concrete step will you take this week to correct it?
?
When you encounter a conflict between a religious text and your rational understanding, what is your immediate reaction? Does it match the Hashwiyya's rigidity, the philosophers' overconfidence, or the Ahl al-Sunna's reconciliation? How can you train yourself to seek synthesis rather than choosing one side?
?
Ghazali says that both extremes come from 'weakness of intellects and lack of insights'. Which extreme are you most vulnerable to? Write down one specific situation where you fell into that extreme, and commit to one action that will help you stay on the straight path next time.

Reason as Eye, Revelation as Sun
Ghazali uses rhetorical questions and analogies to illustrate the interdependence of reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the complementary roles of reason and revelation through Ghazali's vivid analogies and rhetorical questions.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are like a healthy eye and sunlight: each is necessary for true vision.

Ghazali deepens his argument by posing rhetorical questions and offering striking analogies. He shows that reason is needed to verify revelation, yet reason alone is limited. Using the imagery of an eye and the sun, he demonstrates that relying on either alone leads to failure. This lesson explores these powerful metaphors and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the rhetorical questions
Read the three rhetorical questions Ghazali poses. Each challenges an extreme position. Identify what each question argues against.
The questions target those who reject reason, those who reject revelation, and those who think reason is self-sufficient.
2
Understand the analogy of the eye and the sun
Ghazali compares reason to a sound eye and the Qur'an to the sun. Think about how each element contributes to sight and what happens if one is missing.
A closed eye cannot see the sun, and a one-eyed person lacks depth perception.
3
Grasp the conclusion: light upon light
Ghazali ends by stating that reason and revelation together form 'light upon light'. Reflect on why combination is superior.
This phrase alludes to Quranic imagery (Surah Nur).

فالعقل مع الشرع نور على نور، والملاحظ بالعين العوراء لأحدهما على الخصوص متدل بحبل غرور

أهل السنة هم وسيتضح لك أيها المتشوف إلى الاطلاع على قواعد عقائد أهل السنة، الموفقون للجمع المقترح تحقيقها بقواطع الأدلة: أنه لم يستأثر بالتوفيق للجمع بين الشرع بينهما
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, and by Him we seek help.

The Shaykh, the Imam, the Proof of Islam, Abu Hamid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify his soul, said:

Praise be to Allah who chose from the elite of His servants the party of truth and the people of the Sunnah, and distinguished them among all sects with the merits of kindness and grace, and poured upon them from the light of His guidance that by which He uncovered for them the realities of religion, and made their tongues speak with His proof by which He suppressed the misguidance of the atheists, and purified their consciences from the whisperings of devils, and cleansed their hearts from the insinuations of the deviators, and filled their hearts with the lights of certainty; until they were guided thereby to the secrets of what He revealed upon the tongue of His Prophet and chosen one, Muhammad, the master of the messengers, may Allah bless him and all his family. So they came to know the way of reconciling between the requirements of the laws and the demands of the intellects, and they realized that there is no contradiction between transmitted revelation and rational truth. And they knew that those among the Hashwiyya who thought that it is obligatory to rigidly adhere to tradition and follow [their] exaggeration—they have only come from weakness of intellects and lack of insights. And that those among the philosophers and the extremists of the Mu'tazila who delved deeply into the use of reason until they collided with the decisive proofs of the Sharia—they have only come from [deficiency of] insights.

So the inclination of the former is towards negligence, and the inclination of the latter is towards excess, and both are far from caution and prudence. Rather, the necessary obligation in the foundations of belief is to adhere to the middle way and to be steadfast on the straight path, for either extreme of affairs is blameworthy.

The necessity of the interdependence of reason—and how can right guidance be established for one who is content with blindly following transmitted tradition and denies the methods of investigation and reflection according to the people of consideration and insight? Does he not know that there is no basis for the Sharia except the speech of the master of mankind, and rational proof is what affirmed his truthfulness in what he reported?

And how can one be guided to correctness who follows pure reason exclusively, and does not seek illumination from the light of the Sharia nor gain insight?

Would that I knew; how can one resort to reason when it is afflicted by incapacity and confusion? Does he not know that the steps of reason are limited, and its field is narrow and restricted?

Far, far from it! He has certainly failed, with utter loss and ruin, and stumbled in the skirts of misguidance, whoever does not combine reason and revelation to unite this dispersion.

So the example of reason is the sound eye free from defects and diseases, and the example of the Qur'an is the sun spreading light. So how fitting it is for the seeker of guidance who dispenses with one of them in favor of the other to be among the foolish. For one who turns away from reason, contenting himself with the Qur'an, is like one who exposes himself to the sunlight with closed eyelids—there is no difference between him and the blind.

Thus reason along with revelation is light upon light, and whoever observes only one of them with a one-eyed vision clings to a rope of delusion.

The people of the Sunnah—and it will become clear to you, O aspirant to learn the foundations of the beliefs of the people of the Sunnah—are those who are granted success in combining them, as it is sought to be verified by decisive proofs: that no one is singled out for success in combining between them.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of Ghazali's introduction (خطبة الكتاب) to his work on Islamic doctrine. He first praises Allah for selecting the group of truth and the Sunnah (Ahl al-Sunna) and endowing them with the ability to reconcile the demands of divine law and rational thought. Ghazali asserts that there is no real contradiction between transmitted revelation and rational truth. He then critiques two extreme groups: the Hashwiyya, who rigidly cling to tradition and reject reason, and the philosophers and extreme Mu'tazila, who over-rely on reason to the point of opposing definitive revealed texts. Both groups are blamed for lacking insight. He calls for the middle path (الاقتصاد) and steadfastness on the straight path. He provides three rhetorical questions to demonstrate that reason is necessary to verify the truthfulness of the Prophet, that pure reason without revelation is insufficient, and that reason alone has limits. He uses vivid analogies: reason is like a sound eye, the Qur'an like the sun; one who relies solely on the Qur'an without reason is like a person closing his eyes to the sun, and one who relies solely on reason without revelation is like a one-eyed observer holding a rope of delusion. The passage concludes by stating that the people of the Sunnah are the ones who successfully combine both sources.

Key Terms
عقل
شرع
نور
بصيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reason and revelation can function independently and each alone is sufficient for guidance.
Correction: Ghazali argues that reason needs revelation to be guided and revelation needs reason to be properly understood; both are interdependent.

Checkpoint
In Ghazali's analogy, what does the Qur'an represent?
A) A sound eye
B) The sun
C) A rope of delusion
D) Light upon light

Key Takeaway
Ghazali uses vivid analogies to show that reason and revelation are complementary and inseparable for true guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you actively engage your intellect to reflect on its meanings, or do you passively recite? If the latter, what will you change starting this evening's prayer?
?
Think of a time you relied solely on your own reasoning to make a decision without seeking guidance from revelation. Did that lead to confusion? What step can you take this week to ensure you combine both?
?
The analogy of closing one's eyes to the sun is stark. Is there a question about your faith that you have avoided asking out of fear? What would it mean to open your eyes and seek an answer with both reason and revelation?

The Necessity of Combining Reason and Revelation
Al-Ghazali argues for the necessary complementarity of reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Ghazali insists that true guidance requires integrating both rational proof and revealed law.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are light upon light, not enemies.

Al-Ghazali opens his discussion by addressing a common tension in Islamic thought: should one rely solely on reason or solely on transmitted tradition? He argues that both extremes are misguided. In this passage, he lays the foundation for his methodology by demonstrating that reason is necessary to authenticate revelation, and revelation is necessary to guide reason beyond its limits.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to grasp the main argument. Notice the rhetorical questions and analogies.
Pay attention to the tone—Ghazali is both critical and inspiring.
2
Identify the two extreme positions
Find where Ghazali criticizes those who rely only on tradition and those who rely only on reason. Note the phrases he uses to describe each.
3
Understand the eyesight-sunlight analogy
Focus on the analogy: reason is like healthy eyesight, the Quran is like sunlight. Why does he say that combining them is 'light upon light'?
Think about how eyesight needs light to see, and light needs eyes to be perceived.
4
Connect to Ahl al-Sunna
Ghazali presents Ahl al-Sunna as those who successfully combine reason and revelation. Reflect on why this balance is central to Sunni orthodoxy.
This sets the stage for the rest of the book.

ضرورة تلازم العقل وأنَّى يستتب الرشاد لمن يقنع بتقليد الأثر والخبر ، وينكر مناهج البحث والنقل عند أهل النظر والنظر ؟! أولا يعلم أنَّه لا مستند للشرع إلا قول سيد البشر ، وبرهان العقل هو الذي عَرَّفَ صدقَهُ فيما أخبر ؟! وكيف يهتدي للصواب من اقتفى محض العقل واقتصر ، وما استضاءَ بنور الشرع ولا استبصر ؟! فليت شعري ؛ كيف يفزع إلى العقل حيث يعتريه العِيُّ والحَصَرُ ؟! أَوَلا يعلم أنَّ خُطا العقل قاصرة ، وأن مجاله ضيق منحصر ؟! هيهات هيهات قد خاب على القطع والبنات ، وتعثر بأذيال الضلالات .. من لم يجمع بتأليف العقل والشرع هذا الشتات فمثال العقل البصرُ السليم عن الآفات والأدواء ، ومثال القرآن الشمسُ المنتشرة الضياء، فأخلق بأن يكون طالب الاهتداء، المستغني بأحدهما عن الآخر في غمار الأغبياء؛ فالمعرضُ عن العقل اكتفاء المتعرِّضُ لنور الشمس مغمضاً للأجفان، فلا فرق بينه وبين العُميان؛ العقل مع الشرع نور على نور، والملاحِظُ بالعين العوراء لأحدهما على الخصوص متدل بحبل غرور • أهل السنة هم وسيتضح لك أيها المتشوّفُ إلى الاطلاع على قواعد عقائد أهل السنة، الموفقون للجمع المقترح تحقيقها بقواطع الأدلة : أنه لم يستأثر بالتوفيق للجمع بين الشرع = ولا تك فيها مفرطاً أو مُفَرِّطاً كلا طرفي قصد الأمور ذميم . فاشكر الله تعالى على اقتفائِكَ لآثارهم، وانخراطك في سلك نظامهم ودخولك في غمارهم، واختلاطك بفرقتهم، فعساك أن تحشر يومَ القيامة في زمرتهم. نسألُ الله تعالى أن يصفي أسرارنا عن كدورات الضلال، ويغمرها بنور الحقيقة، وأن يخرس ألسنتنا عن النطق بالباطل، وينطقها بالحق والحكمة، إنَّه الكريم الفائض المنَّة، الواسع الرحمة.
The necessity of the correlation of reason. How can guidance be established for one who is content with following tradition and reports, and denies the methods of investigation and transmission according to the people of examination and reflection?! Does he not know that there is no basis for the Law except the statement of the master of mankind, and the rational proof is what made known his truthfulness in what he reported?! How can one who follows pure reason exclusively be guided to what is correct, without being illuminated by the light of the Law or seeing clearly?! Would that I knew: how can one resort to reason when it is afflicted with incapacity and confusion?! Does he not know that the steps of reason are limited, and its field is narrow and restricted?! Far, far! He has surely failed conclusively, and stumbled in the skirts of misguidance, whoever does not combine reason and Law to unify this scattered state. The example of reason is sound eyesight free from defects and ailments, and the example of the Quran is the sun spreading its light. How fitting that the seeker of guidance who dispenses with one of them in favor of the other be among the foolish! For the one who turns away from reason in contentment, like one who exposes himself to sunlight with eyelids closed, there is no difference between him and the blind. Reason with the Law is light upon light, and the one who looks with a one-eyed eye at either one in particular is holding on to a rope of delusion. The people of the Sunna – and it will become clear to you, O one eager to learn the principles of the beliefs of the people of the Sunna, they are those who are given success in combining [the two], and it is proposed to verify this by decisive proofs – that no one else has been singled out for success in combining the Law and reason. Do not be extreme or negligent in this matter; both extremes of a matter are blameworthy. So thank God Almighty for your following their traces, and your joining their system, and your entering among their multitude, and your mixing with their group; perhaps you will be resurrected on the Day of Judgment in their company. We ask God Almighty to purify our innermost thoughts from the turbidities of misguidance, and to immerse them in the light of truth, and to silence our tongues from speaking falsehood, and to make them speak truth and wisdom. Indeed, He is the Generous, the Bestower of favor, the Vast in mercy.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a methodological prologue in which Al-Ghazali argues for the necessary complementarity of reason and revelation. He begins by criticizing two extremes: those who rely solely on transmitted tradition (taqlīd) and reject rational investigation, and those who rely solely on reason and ignore revelation. He points out that the authority of revelation itself rests on rational proof that establishes the truthfulness of the Prophet. Then he refutes the notion that reason can be self-sufficient by noting its limitations: reason is finite and prone to confusion. He declares that failure is certain for anyone who does not combine reason and Law. Ghazali then uses two powerful analogies: reason is like healthy eyesight, the Quran is like sunlight; each alone is insufficient—eyesight cannot see in darkness, and sunlight is useless without eyes. The one who tries to use only one is like a person closing his eyes to the sun, equivalent to blindness. He then introduces the saved group: Ahl al-Sunna, who successfully combine both sources using decisive proofs. He urges the reader to follow them, avoid extremism in either direction, and offers a concluding supplication for purification and guidance.

Misconception: Reason and revelation are inherently opposed and cannot be reconciled.
Correction: Al-Ghazali argues they are complementary: reason authenticates revelation, and revelation guides reason beyond its limitations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

If reason and revelation seem to conflict in your mind, are you willing to honestly reconsider your interpretation rather than reject either?
?
Al-Ghazali says the one who abandons reason is like a person closing his eyes to the sun. In what area of your life are you 'closing your eyes'—refusing to think deeply or ask hard questions—while still claiming to follow the light of revelation? What would it cost you to open your eyes?

The Structure and Purpose of al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad
Ghazali defines the title and structure of his book, outlining four introductions and four poles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the bipartite structure of Ghazali's al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad, consisting of four introductory discussions and four main poles, and the unified perspective that ties them together.

Core Idea
Ghazali's book is a moderate path to understanding God, built on four foundations and four pillars.

Before diving into the arguments of al-Iqtisad, Ghazali takes care to lay out the blueprint of the book. He explains what the title means and how the work is organized: four preliminary introductions (tamhidat) followed by four core poles (aqtab). This lesson explores that structure and the specific focus that each pole brings to the study of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall flow. Notice how Ghazali first gives the title, then describes the two-part structure.
2
Identify the introductions
List the four introductions. Note that they are not the main content but serve as groundwork and justification for the science of kalam.
The introductions are enumerated explicitly.
3
Examine the poles
Read the description of the four poles. Observe that Ghazali says they are 'confined to considering God,' and that each pole examines a specific subject (world, prophet, statements) from a theological angle.
Only three poles are described in this excerpt.
4
Reflect on the unified perspective
Consider why Ghazali insists on looking at everything 'from the aspect of God' or 'from the aspect of being God's work/messenger/definition.' How does this unify the book?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في التعريف بهذا الكتاب ولنفتح الكلام ببيان اسم الكتاب وتقسيم المقدمات والفصول والأبواب . أما اسم الكتاب فهو : « الاقتصاد في الاعتقاد » وأما ترتيبه : فهو مشتمل على أربعة تمهيدات تجري مجرى التوطئة والمقدمات ، وعلى أربعة أقطاب تجري مجرى المقاصد والغايات . التمهيد الأوّل : في بيان أن هذا العلم من المهمّاتِ في الدِّين . التمهيد الثاني : في بيان أنه ليس مهمّاً لجميع المسلمين ، بل لطائفة منهم مخصوصين . التمهيد الثالث : في بيان أنه من فروض الكفايات ، لا من فروض الأعيان . التمهيد الرابع : في تفصيل مناهج الأدلَّةِ التي أوردتها في هذا الكتاب . وأما الأقطاب المقصودة .. فأربعةٌ ، وجملتها مقصورة على النظر في الله تعالى : فإنَّا إن نظرنا في العالم .. لم ننظر فيه من حيث إنه عالم وجسم وسماء وأرض ، بل من حيث إنه صنع الله . وإن نظرنا في النبي .. لم ننظر فيه من حيث إنه إنسان وشريف وعالم وفاضل ، بل من حيث إنَّه رسولُ الله . وإن نظرنا في أقواله .. لم ننظر فيها من حيث إنها أقوال ومخاطبات وتفهيمات ، بل من حيث إنّها تعريف بواسطتِهِ من الله تعالى
Chapter on the definition of this book. And we shall open the discourse by explaining the name of the book and the division of its introductions, sections, and chapters. As for the name of the book, it is 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' (The Moderation in Belief). As for its arrangement, it includes four introductions (tamhidat) that serve as preliminaries and prolegomena, and four poles (aqtab) that serve as purposes and ends. The first introduction: on explaining that this knowledge is among the important matters in religion. The second introduction: on explaining that it is not important for all Muslims, but rather for a specific group among them. The third introduction: on explaining that it is among the communal obligations (furuḍ al-kifāyāt), not individual obligations (furuḍ al-a'yān). The fourth introduction: on detailing the methods of proofs that I have presented in this book. As for the intended poles, they are four, and their totality is confined to considering God Almighty. For if we look at the world, we do not look at it from the aspect that it is a world, a body, a sky, or an earth, but rather from the aspect that it is the handiwork of God. If we look at the Prophet, we do not look at him from the aspect that he is a human, a noble, a scholar, or a virtuous person, but rather from the aspect that he is the Messenger of God. If we look at his statements, we do not look at them from the aspect that they are statements, speeches, or communications, but rather from the aspect that they are a definition through his mediation from God Almighty.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction in which Imam al-Ghazali defines the title and organization of his book. He announces the subject is the definition of the book itself. The title is 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' (The Moderation in Belief), indicating a balanced, middle-path approach. The book's arrangement is bipartite: there are four preliminary discussions (tamhidat) and four main poles (aqtab). The introductions serve as groundwork; the poles are the ultimate objectives.

He then enumerates the four introductions:
1. The first introduction establishes the importance of this science (ʿilm al-kalām) in religion.
2. The second clarifies that it is not obligatory for all Muslims, only for specific qualified persons.
3. The third states that it is a communal obligation (fard kifāya), not an individual obligation (fard ʿayn), meaning if some fulfill it, the rest are absolved.
4. The fourth details the methods of proofs used in the book.

Then he describes the four poles. They are all confined to the consideration of God (al-naẓar fī Llāh taʿālā). However, the subject matter of each pole is approached from a specific perspective:
- When looking at the world, the focus is not on its physical attributes but on its being the creation (ṣunʿ) of God.
- When looking at the Prophet, the focus is not on his human qualities but on his being the Messenger of God.
- When looking at the Prophet's statements, the focus is not on their linguistic nature but on their being a means of definition (taʿrīf) from God through him.

This passage thus sets out the structural framework of the entire work and the special perspective that will govern each discussion.

Key Terms
اقتصاد في الاعتقاد
تمهيد
قطب
نظر
فرض كفاية
فرض عين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the four poles are about the world, the Prophet, and his statements as separate topics.
Correction: They are all unified under the single consideration of God, as each is examined from a theological perspective.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, how should we look at the world in this book?
A) From the aspect that it is a body, sky, and earth
B) From the aspect that it is the handiwork of God

D) From the aspect that it contains signs for the learned

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad is structured with four preparatory introductions and four main poles, all centered on a theological consideration of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the world around you—your career, your home, nature—do you see them as mere objects and activities, or as the handiwork of God? What would change in your daily life if you genuinely saw everything as God's creation?
?
Ghazali says that this deep theological knowledge is not for all Muslims, but for a specific group. Are you avoiding it because you think it's not your responsibility, or are you among those who should seek it? What is stopping you from studying theology seriously?
?
The Prophet and his statements, according to Ghazali, should ultimately point you to God, not stop at themselves. Do you love the Prophet for his own sake or as a means to know God? How can you shift your focus from the messenger to the One who sent him?

Book Title and Four Preliminaries
Ghazali states the book's title and lists the four introductory preliminaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the title of Ghazali's work and the four introductory preliminaries that set the stage for the entire book.

Core Idea
The structure of a book reveals its purpose; Ghazali's preliminaries define the aim and scope of his theological method.

In this opening passage, Ghazali introduces his book 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' (Moderation in Belief) and outlines the four foundational preliminaries that will guide the reader. He clarifies the importance of the science of kalam, its target audience, its status as a communal obligation, and the methodology of proofs used. This sets the framework for all that follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components
Notice Ghazali begins by naming the book and then dividing it into preliminaries and main poles. Identify the four preliminaries listed.
2
Understand the first preliminary
The science of kalam is important in religion. Ask yourself: why is it important?
3
Discern the audience
The second preliminary narrows the importance to a specific group. Who are they? The commentary suggests those capable of reasoning.
4
Classify the obligation
The third preliminary distinguishes communal vs. individual obligation. This is a key distinction in Islamic jurisprudence.
5
Note the methodological fourth
The fourth preliminary details the proofs used. This shows Ghazali's systematic approach.

Chapter on definition of this [book]. Let us begin the discourse by explaining the name of the book, and the division of the introductions, chapters, and the book, and the sections. As for the name of the book, it is 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad'. As for its arrangement, it includes four preliminaries (tamhidat) which serve as introductions and premises, and four poles (aqtab) which serve as objectives and ends. The first preliminary: on explaining that this science is among the important matters in religion. The second preliminary: on explaining that it is not important for all Muslims, but only for a specific group of them. The third preliminary: on explaining that it is a communal obligation (fard kifaya), not an individual obligation (fard 'ayn). The fourth preliminary: on detailing the methods of proofs that I have employed in this book.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage opens the book with a definition of its own structure. Ghazali first gives the title: 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' (The Moderation in Belief). He then explains the arrangement: the book is composed of four preliminaries (tamhidat) that serve as introductions, and four poles (aqtab) that serve as the main objectives. The four preliminaries are then listed. The first explains that this science (i.e., kalam) is important in religion. The second specifies that it is not important for all Muslims, but only for a specific group—likely those capable of reasoning. The third states that it is a communal obligation, not an individual obligation, meaning that if some qualified persons undertake it, the rest are absolved. The fourth outlines the methodology of proofs used in the book. This sets the stage for the entire work.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that every Muslim is individually obligated to study kalam (theology) in depth.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly states that this science is a communal obligation (fard kifaya), meaning that if a sufficient number of qualified people engage in it, the rest of the community is absolved from the obligation.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' begins by framing the study of kalam as an important, communal pursuit for a specific group, with a clear methodological structure.

?

?
When you read the title 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad' (Moderation in Belief), do you see moderation reflected in your own beliefs? Are there areas of extremism or negligence you need to address?

The Four Poles: All Theology Centers on God
Ghazali introduces the four poles as the sole subjects of theological inquiry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali reduces all theological considerations to four poles centered on God.

Core Idea
All theology is about God — nothing else.

Imam al-Ghazali begins by setting the scope of his work. He wants to make it clear that every topic in kalam, whether about the world, the Prophet, or his statements, is ultimately a consideration of God. This grounding prevents the student from losing focus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how Ghazali reorients each topic toward God.
2
Identify the pattern of reorientation
Ghazali takes three examples — the world, the Prophet, and his statements — and shows that in each case, we disregard the thing's own nature and consider only its relation to God. Observe the phrase "لا ننظر فيه من حيث إنه... بل من حيث إنه".
This pattern is the key to understanding his methodology.
3
List the four poles
At the end of the passage, Ghazali enumerates the four poles: God's essence, attributes, actions, and the messenger with the definition of God. Write them down.
These four poles will structure the entire science.
4
Reflect on the unity of the science
Consider why the Prophet and his statements are included as a pole. How does the definition of God via the messenger relate to the other three poles?
This shows that revelation is integral to theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأقطاب المقصودة .. فأربعةٌ ، وجملتها مقصورة على النظر في الله تعالى : فإنَّا إن نظرنا في العالم .. لم ننظر فيه من حيث إنه عالم وجسم وسماء وأرض ، بل من حيث إنه صنع الله وإن نظرنا في النبي .. لم ننظر فيه من حيث إنه إنسان وشريف وعالم وفاضل ، بل من حيث إنَّه رسولُ الله وإن نظرنا في أقواله .. لم ننظر فيها من حيث إنها أقوال ومخاطبات وتفهميات ، بل من حيث إنّها تعريف بواسطتِهِ من الله تعالى فلا نظرَ إلا في الله ، ولا مطلوب سوى الله ، وجميع أطراف هذا العلم يحصرُهُ النظر في ذات الله ، وفي صفات الله ، وفي أفعال الله ، وفي رسول الله وما جاءنا على لسانه من تعريف الله فهي إذن أربعة أقطاب :
As for the intended poles—there are four, and their totality is confined to consideration of God, exalted: For if we consider the world, we do not consider it insofar as it is a world, a body, a sky, or an earth, but insofar as it is the handiwork of God. And if we consider the Prophet, we do not consider him insofar as he is a human, noble, learned, or virtuous, but insofar as he is the messenger of God. And if we consider his statements, we do not consider them insofar as they are statements, addresses, or communications, but insofar as they are a definition by means of him from God, exalted. So there is no consideration except of God, and no object of quest except God. All aspects of this science are encompassed by the consideration of God's essence, God's attributes, God's actions, and the messenger of God and what has come to us from his tongue of the definition of God. So they are four poles:
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage explains the unifying theme of the four poles. Ghazali emphasizes that every topic in the book is subordinated to the consideration of God. For example, when we look at the world, we do not study it as a physical object but as God's creation. When we study the Prophet, we focus on his role as messenger, not his human qualities. When we study the Prophet's sayings, we treat them as a means through which God defines Himself. Therefore, all considerations reduce to four: God's essence, attributes, actions, and His messenger (who brings knowledge of God). This sets the scope for the entire work.

رسول الله
تعريف الله

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam covers many unrelated topics like cosmology, prophethood, etc., independently of God.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies that every topic is considered only insofar as it relates to God: the world as His handiwork, the Prophet as His messenger, etc. All reduce to four poles about God.

According to Ghazali, why do we consider the Prophet in this science?
A) Because he is a noble human
B) Because he is the messenger of God

D) Because he is learned

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How would your daily awareness change if you truly saw everything as a sign of His power and wisdom? Commit to pausing before the end of today and reflecting on one thing you normally take for granted as a created sign of God.
?
In your study of religion, what topics do you tend to focus on that are not directly about God? Are you willing to re-center every subject—history, ethics, law—to see how it points to God? Before you read or listen to any religious talk this week, ask yourself: 'How does this bring me closer to knowing God?'
?
Ghazali says that even the Prophet's virtues are not considered for themselves but only as messenger from God. Do you honor the Prophet in a way that leads you to God, or do you sometimes stop at admiration of his character? Pray that your love for the Prophet becomes a means, not an end, and that it increases your desire to know God.

The Four Poles of the Science of Kalam
Ghazali divides kalam into four poles and enumerates their contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ghazali divides the entire subject matter of kalam into four comprehensive poles and what each pole covers.

Core Idea
The entire science of kalam is contained in four poles: God's essence, attributes, acts, and messengers.

Imam al-Ghazali begins his work by providing a clear map of the entire field of kalam. He organizes the subject into four poles that cover everything about God and His relationship to creation. This structural outline will guide the rest of the book, so understanding it is essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow, then read the English translation. Notice how Ghazali introduces the four poles.
The passage is dense with technical terms; don't worry about every detail yet.
2
Identify the four poles
Find where Ghazali says 'فهي إذن أربعة أقطاب' (they are then four poles). Then list each pole and the number of claims or chapters under it.
The first pole has ten claims, the third has seven, the fourth has four chapters.
3
Notice the logical progression
Observe how Ghazali moves from God's essence (what He is) to His attributes (how He is described) to His acts (what He does) to His messengers (how He communicates). This sequence is deliberate.
4
Reflect on the inclusiveness
Consider why the fourth pole includes not only prophethood but also eschatology and imamate. Ask yourself: does this cover everything a Muslim theologian needs to defend?
This ties back to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا نظرَ إلا في الله ، ولا مطلوب سوى الله ، وجميع أطراف هذا العلم يحصرُهُ النظر في ذات الله ، وفي صفات الله ، وفي أفعال الله ، وفي رسول الله وما جاءنا على لسانه من تعريف الله فهي إذن أربعة أقطاب : القطب الأول : النظر في ذات الله تعالى : فنبين فيه وجودَهُ ، وأنه قديم ، وأنه باقي ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ، ولا جسم ، ولا عرض ، ولا محدود بحد ، ولا هو مخصوص بجهةٍ ، وأنه مرئي كما أنه معلوم ، وأنه واحد فهذه عشر دعاوى نبيتها في هذا القطب إن شاء الله تعالى القطب الثاني : في صفات الله تعالى : ونبيِّنُ فيه أنَّه حيٌّ ، عالم ، قادر ، مريد ، سميع ، بصير ، متكلم وأنَّ له حياةً ، وعلماً ، وقدرة ، وإرادة ، وسمعاً ، وبصراً ، وكلاماً . ونذكرُ أحكام هذه الصفات ولوازمها ، وما يفترقُ فيها وما يجتمع فيها من الأحكام ، وأنَّ هذه الصفات زائدة على الذات ، وقديمة وقائمة بالذات ، ولا يجوز أن يكون شيء من الصفات حادثاً القطب الثالث : في أفعال الله تعالى : وفيه سبع دعاوى ، وهو أنَّه لا يجب على الله تعالى التكليف ، ولا الخلق ، ولا الثوابُ على التكليف ، ولا رعاية صلاح العباد ، ولا يستحيل منه تكليف ما لا يطاق، ولا يجب عليه العقاب على المعاصي ، ولا يستحيلُ منه بعثة الأنبياء ، بل يجوز ذلك وفي مقدمة هذا القطب بيان معنى الواجب والحسن والقبيح . القطب الرابع : في رسل الله ، وما جاءَ على لسان رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الحشر والنشر ، والجنة والنار ، والشفاعة ، وعذاب القبر ، والميزان ، والصراط • وفيه أربعة أبواب : الباب الأول : في إثبات نبوَّة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . الباب الثاني : فيما ورد على لسانه صلى الله عليه وسلم من أمور الآخرة . الباب الثالث : في الإمامة وشروطها الباب الرابع : في بيان القانون في تكفيرِ الفِرَقِ المُبتدعة
Thus there is no consideration except concerning God, and no sought object except God, and all aspects of this science are encompassed by consideration of God's Essence, and of God's Attributes, and of God's Acts, and of God's Messenger and what came to us upon his tongue of definition from God. So they are then four poles: The first pole: Consideration of God's Essence, may He be exalted: we explain therein His existence, that He is eternal, that He is everlasting, that He is not a substance, nor a body, nor an accident, nor bounded by a boundary, nor is He particularized by a direction, and that He is visible just as He is known, and that He is one. These are ten claims we will explain in this pole, God willing. The second pole: Concerning God's Attributes, may He be exalted: we explain therein that He is living, knowing, powerful, willing, hearing, seeing, speaking, and that He has life, knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, and speech. And we mention the rulings of these attributes and their necessary concomitants, and what differs and what agrees among them in terms of rulings, and that these attributes are additional to the essence, eternal and subsisting in the essence, and it is not permissible that any of the attributes be originated. The third pole: Concerning God's Acts, may He be exalted: therein are seven claims, namely that God is not obligated to impose obligation, nor to create, nor to reward for obligation, nor to observe the welfare of servants, nor is it impossible from Him to impose what is beyond capacity, nor is He obligated to punish for disobedience, nor is it impossible from Him to send prophets; rather that is permissible. And in the introduction to this pole is an explanation of the meaning of obligatory, good, and evil. The fourth pole: Concerning God's messengers, and what came upon the tongue of His Messenger, peace be upon him, regarding resurrection and dispersal, paradise and hell, intercession, punishment of the grave, the balance, and the path. It contains four chapters: Chapter one: On proving the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him. Chapter two: On what came upon his tongue, peace be upon him, of matters of the afterlife. Chapter three: On the imamate and its conditions. Chapter four: On clarifying the rule regarding declaring misguided sects as unbelievers.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a structural outline in which Imam al-Ghazali divides the entire subject matter of 'ilm al-kalam into four main poles (aqṭāb). He begins by stating that the entire science is confined to considering God Himself—His essence, attributes, acts, and His messenger—and then enumerates each pole with its specific topics. The first pole covers ten claims regarding God's essence: existence, eternality, everlastingness, that He is not a substance, body, accident, bounded, or in a direction, that He is visible and one. The second pole deals with the seven essential attributes (life, knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, speech) and their properties: that they are additional to the essence, eternal, subsisting, and cannot be originated. The third pole presents seven claims about God's acts: that He is not obligated to create, impose obligation, reward, or ensure welfare; that imposing the impossible is not impossible for Him; that He is not obligated to punish; and that sending prophets is permissible (not necessary). A preface on the meanings of 'obligatory', 'good', and 'evil' is included. The fourth pole concerns the messengers, specifically the resurrection, paradise, hell, intercession, grave punishment, balance, and path, and it has four chapters: proof of Muhammad's prophethood, afterlife matters, imamate and its conditions, and the ruling on takfir of innovated sects. This division provides a comprehensive roadmap for the whole work.

Key Terms

ذات الله
صفات الله
أفعال الله
رسل الله
دعاوى
أبواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these four poles are mutually exclusive or sequential topics that can be studied independently.
Correction: Ghazali treats them as an exhaustive and interrelated structure covering all topics of kalam, not as separate disciplines.

Checkpoint

B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Ghazali organizes the science of kalam into four poles: essence, attributes, acts, and messengers, each with specific claims and chapters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study Islamic theology, do you truly seek God Himself, or do you treat it as an intellectual exercise to satisfy your own curiosity? How will you realign your intention starting today?

Which of these four poles—God's essence, attributes, acts, or messengers—do you feel least connected to in your daily life? What is one concrete action you will take this week to deepen your understanding and love for that aspect of your faith?
?
Ghazali says all of kalam revolves around God. Yet we often study topics like the afterlife or imamate as separate subjects. Are you living as if the Hereafter is real and imminent? What would change in your schedule or habits if you truly believed every moment brings you closer to resurrection?

The Pursuit of Eternal Happiness and Prophetic Miracles
Ghazali states the importance of focusing on eternal salvation and the role of prophets with miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali considers the pursuit of eternal happiness the most important goal and how the claims of prophets, supported by miracles, compel a rational person to investigate.

Core Idea
Eternal happiness is the ultimate aim, and prophetic miracles demand investigation.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali lays the foundational principle for his entire theological project: human beings must prioritize their eternal fate over worldly concerns. He argues that prophets have not only informed us of divine duties but have supported their message with unmistakable miracles, which naturally disturb the seeker's complacency and drive them to inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Familiarize yourself with Ghazali's argument about the priority of eternal happiness and the role of prophets. Pay attention to the rhetorical force of his language.
The passage is dense but crucial for understanding the motivation behind kalam.
2
Identify the key concepts
Note how Ghazali contrasts eternal happiness with wasting time, and how he describes the psychological impact of hearing about miracles. Terms like 'dhan badihi' (intuitive opinion) and 'tajwiz daruri' (necessary possibility) are important.
3
Reflect on why this matters
Understand why Ghazali starts his book with this focus on the afterlife and the need for verification. This sets the stage for his arguments on prophethood and the necessity of kalam.
This principle underlies the entire discipline of ‘aqida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أنَّ صرف الهمَّة إلى ما ليس بمهم ، وتضييع الزمان بما عنه بد. الحذر من تضيع غاية الضلال ونهاية الخسران ، سواء كان المنصرَفُ إليه بالهمة : من العلوم ، أم من الأعمال ؛ فنعوذُ بالله من علم لا ينفع هو وأهم الأمور لكافة الخلق نيل السعادة الأبدية ، واجتناب الشقاوة البحث عن السعادة الدائمة ، وقد ورد الأنبياء وأخبروا الخلق بأن الله تعالى على عباده حقوقاً ووظائف في أفعالهم وأقوالهم وعقائدهم ، وأنَّ من لم ينطق بالصدق لسانه ، ولم ينطوِ على الحقِّ ضميره ، ولم تتزيَّن بالعمل جوارحه .. فمصيره إلى النار ، وعاقبته البوار . غاية المرام ثم لم يقتصروا على مجرَّدِ الإخبار ، بل استشهدوا على صدقهم بأمور تني[؟]ة الــرســـول بمعجزته العقل غريبة ، وأفعال عجيبة خارقة للعادات ، خارجة عن مقدورات البشر ، فمن شاهدها أو سمعَ أحوالها بالأخبار المتواترة.. سبق إلى عقله إمكان صدقهم ، بل غلب على ظنه ذلك بأوّل السماع قبل أن يمعن النظر في تمييز المعجزاتِ عن عجائب الصناعات ، وهذا الظن البديهي أو التجويز الضروري ينزِعُ الطمأنينة عن القلب ، ويخشوه بالاستشعار والخوف . ويهيجه للبحث والافتكار ، ويسلب عنه الدَّعَةَ والقرار ، ويحذِّرُهُ مغبة التساهل والإهمال ، ويقرُرُ عنده أنَّ الموتَ آتِ لا محالة ، وأنَّ ما بعد الموت منطو عن أبصار الخلق ، وأنَّ ما أخبر به هؤلاء غير خارج عن حيز الإمكان
Know: directing effort to what is not important, and wasting time on what one can avoid, is the extreme of error and the end of loss, whether the object of effort is of sciences or deeds; so we seek refuge with Allah from knowledge that does not benefit. And the most important of matters for all creatures is attaining eternal happiness and avoiding perpetual misery by seeking lasting happiness. The prophets came and informed the creatures that Allah the Exalted has rights and duties upon His servants in their deeds, words, and beliefs, and that whoever does not speak truth with his tongue, does not interiorize truth in his conscience, and does not adorn his limbs with good deeds—his destiny is the Fire and his end is ruin. The ultimate aim. Then they did not content themselves with mere informing, but they testified to their truthfulness by matters that indicate[?] the messenger by his intellectual[?] miracle, strange acts contrary to custom, beyond human capability. So whoever witnessed them or heard reports of them through recurrent reports (mutawatir)—there springs to his mind the possibility of their truthfulness, rather it becomes his predominant opinion at first hearing before he deeply investigates distinguishing miracles from extraordinary human crafts. This intuitive opinion or necessary possibility removes tranquility from the heart, instills it with apprehension and fear, rouses it to research and reflection, strips it of ease and rest, warns it of the consequence of negligence and carelessness, and establishes in it that death is inevitably coming, and that what comes after death is hidden from the sight of creation, and that what these [prophets] have informed of is not beyond the realm of possibility.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction. Ghazali begins by condemning wasting effort on unimportant matters, whether in sciences or actions, and then states that the most important goal for all people is eternal salvation. The prophets have informed humanity of God's rights and duties, and of the punishment for those who disbelieve or disobey. They did not merely claim this but supported their truthfulness with miracles (mu'jizat) that are beyond human power. When one witnesses or hears of these miracles through overwhelming reports (tawatur), one immediately perceives their possibility, and even forms a dominant opinion of their truth before detailed analysis. This natural initial 'dhan' (opinion) or necessary 'tajwiz' (possibility) disturbs one's complacency and motivates investigation. It instills fear about the afterlife and the fact that death is certain. Thus, the listener is compelled to examine the truth of the prophets' message.

Key Terms

المعجزات
الخبر المتواتر
الظن البديهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that engaging in kalam (theological speculation) is unnecessary or even blameworthy, as it seems to rely on human reasoning rather than simple faith.
Correction: Ghazali argues that because prophets have warned of eternal consequences and supported their messages with miracles, a rational person is naturally compelled to investigate those claims. Thus, far from being a luxury, such inquiry becomes an essential duty to secure one's eternal salvation.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali establishes that the pursuit of eternal happiness, guided by prophetic miracles, is the paramount concern that compels rational inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Ghazali says that the intuitive opinion of the prophets' truth removes tranquility and instills fear. Are you comfortable in your ignorance, or are you actively seeking the truth about eternal happiness? What have you done today to pursue that goal?
?
You know that death is coming, and the afterlife is hidden. Do you live as if that is the most important matter? Or do you waste effort on unimportant things? What would change if you truly prioritized eternal happiness?

The Lion in the House: Necessity of Investigating Prophethood
Ghazali argues via analogy that investigating prophethood is obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that investigating the prophets' message is the most important task, using the analogy of a lion warning.

Core Idea
Even a mere possibility of truth demands investigation when the stakes are infinite.

Ghazali presents a powerful analogy to motivate the search for truth about prophethood. He compares the prophets, who have shown miracles, to a person warning you that a lion has entered your house. Just as you would not ignore such a warning even if it is only possible, you cannot ignore the prophets' message when the afterlife is at stake. This lesson unpacks that analogy and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the original Arabic and the English translation side by side. Notice the rhetorical questions and the emphatic language.
The first line of the page is slightly corrupted; focus on the main argument.
2
Identify the analogy's components
Identify the two sides of the analogy: the prophets and their miracles versus the lion warning. What is the point of comparison?
Both involve a warning of potential harm, with evidence that the claim could be true.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
Ghazali concludes that investigating the prophet's claim is the most important matter. How does the analogy lead to this?
Because death is certain and the afterlife is eternal, the risk is even greater than a lion.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common objection: religious belief isn't like empirical caution. Why does Ghazali think it is analogous?
Both involve acting on a possibility with high stakes; the difference in domain doesn't weaken the logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب انتهاج فالحزم تركُ التواني في الكشف عن حقيقة هذا الأمر ؛ فما هؤلاء (۱) ـ مع - العجائب التي أظهرُوها في إمكان صدقهم قبل البحث عن تحقيق قولهم - بأقل من شخص واحد يخبرنا عند خروجنا من دارنا ومحل استقرارنا بأن سبعاً من السباع قد دخل الدار فخذ حذرك ، واحترز منه لنفسك جهدك . فإنا بمجرد السماع ، إذا رأينا ما أخبر عنه في محل الإمكان والجواز ... لا نقدِمُ على الدخول ، بل نبالغ في الاحتراز ، فالموت هو المستقر والوطن قطعاً ، فكيف لا يكون الاحتراز لما بعده مهماً ؟! فإذن ؛ أهم المهمات أن نبحث عن قوله الذي قضى الذهن في بادىء الرأي وسابق النظر بإمكانه : أهو محال في نفسه على التحقيق ، أو هو حقٌّ لا شك فيه ؟
The necessity of proceeding: determination is leaving laziness in uncovering the reality of this matter. For these [prophets]—with the wonders they have shown concerning the possibility of their truthfulness before investigating the truth of their statement—are no less than a single person who informs us, when we leave our house and our place of residence, that a lion from among the predators has entered the house: 'Take your precaution and guard yourself from it as much as you can.' For we, upon mere hearing, when we see that what he informed about is within the realm of possibility and permissibility, we do not proceed to enter, but rather we exaggerate in taking precautions. Death is the final abode and home definitively, so how could precaution for what comes after it not be important?! Therefore, the most important of important matters is that we investigate his statement—the one which the mind initially, at first sight and prior reflection, deemed possible: is it impossible in itself upon investigation, or is it truth beyond doubt?
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is an argument by analogy. Ghazali asserts that determination requires abandoning laziness to investigate the truth of the prophets' claims. He compares the prophets, who have shown miracles indicating the possibility of their truth, to a single person who warns you that a lion has entered your house. Upon hearing such a warning, even if it is only possible, you would not enter; you would take maximum precautions. Likewise, death is certain and the afterlife is the eternal home, so precaution regarding it is even more important. Therefore, the most important task is to investigate the prophet's message: is it inherently impossible, or is it true beyond doubt? The analogy underscores that even a mere possibility of truth demands investigation, so how much more when there are supporting miracles?

Key Terms

السباع
الموت
الاحتراز
الإمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that caution in worldly matters (like a lion) is based on certainty, whereas religious belief is based on faith, so the analogy fails.
Correction: Ghazali's point is that even a possibility of harm demands caution in worldly matters; the prophets' claim is supported by miracles that make it at least possible, and the stakes (eternal life) are far greater, so the same logic applies.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali compare the prophets' warnings to in this passage?
A) A doctor's advice
B) A traveler's tale
C) A person warning of a lion in the house
D) A king's decree

Key Takeaway
The possibility of a prophet's truth, supported by miracles, demands investigation because the consequences of ignoring it are eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever ignored a warning because it seemed unlikely, only to regret it later? How does that apply to your approach to the message of the Prophet?
?
If a lion were in your house, you would not hesitate to act. Why do you hesitate when it comes to the eternal warning of prophethood? What does that reveal about your priorities?
?
The lesson says the most important matter is to investigate the truth of the prophet's claim. Have you done that investigation sincerely, or have you been lazy? What will you do about it?

The Lion Analogy: Why We Must Investigate Prophetic Claims
Ghazali uses a lion analogy to show the necessity of investigating prophetic claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that the mere possibility of a prophet's truthfulness makes it rationally obligatory to investigate his message.

Core Idea
Even a possible warning demands caution; eternal consequences make investigation urgent.

Imagine someone tells you a lion has entered your house. You wouldn't dismiss it without checking — the risk is too great. Ghazali uses this everyday example to show that the same logic applies to prophetic claims. Since death is certain and the afterlife is at stake, investigating the truth of the prophet's message becomes the most important task.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with the analogy
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the comparison between the lion warning and the prophet's warning. Notice how Ghazali builds the analogy.
The Arabic may have some OCR corruption at the start; focus on the meaning conveyed in the translation.
2
Understand the key terms: إمكان and جواز
These terms refer to possibility and permissibility. In the analogy, the lion report is merely possible — you haven't confirmed it. Yet you still act. Similarly, the prophet's message is at least possible, so you must investigate.
3
Trace the conclusion: from caution to investigation
Ghazali argues that if we take precautions for this life based on a possible danger, we must certainly take precautions for the afterlife — which is certain. Therefore, investigating the prophet's claim is the most important task.
4
Reflect: what the analogy does NOT prove
The analogy does not prove the prophet is truthful. It only shows that the rational response to a possible truth is to investigate. This is methodological, not a proof of prophethood.
This is a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[؟] وجوب انتهاج فالحزم تركُ التواني في الكشف عن حقيقة هذا الأمر؛ فما هؤلاء مع العجائب التي أظهروها في إمكان صدقهم قبل البحث عن تحقيق قولهم بأقل من شخص واحد يخبرنا عند خروجنا من دارنا ومحل استقرارنا بأن سبعاً من السباع قد دخل الدار فخذ حذرك، واحترز منه لنفسك جهدك. فإنا بمجرد السماع، إذا رأينا ما أخبر عنه في محل الإمكان والجواز ... لا نقدم على الدخول، بل نبالغ في الاحتراز، فالموت هو المستقر والوطن قطعاً، فكيف لا يكون الاحتراز لما بعده مهماً؟! فإذن؛ أهم المهمات أن نبحث عن قوله الذي قضى الذهن في بادىء الرأي وسابق النظر بإمكانه: أهو محال في نفسه على التحقيق، أو هو حقٌ لا شك فيه؟
[؟] The obligation to adopt resolution is to abandon negligence in uncovering the truth of this matter. For these people [the prophets] – with the wonders they have shown concerning the possibility of their truthfulness before investigating the verification of their statement – are not less than a single person who informs us, when we leave our house and place of residence, that a lion among the predators has entered the house, so take your precaution and guard yourself from it with all your effort. For we, upon merely hearing, when we see that what he informed about is within the realm of possibility and permissibility ... we do not proceed to enter, rather we exaggerate in caution. Death is the final abode and home definitively, so how could caution for what comes after it not be important?! Therefore, the most important of important matters is that we investigate his statement, which the mind initially judges and in preliminary consideration to be possible: is it impossible in itself upon verification, or is it true without doubt?
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is an analogical argument demonstrating the rational necessity to investigate prophetic claims. The author begins by stating the obligation to adopt resolution and abandon negligence in uncovering the truth. He then compares the prophets to a single person who warns that a lion has entered one's house. Despite the warner's credibility not yet being verified, the mere possibility of danger compels one to take precaution. The author extends this analogy: death is the certain and final abode, so caution for the afterlife is even more important. The conclusion is that the most important matter is to investigate the prophet's statement—specifically, whether it is inherently impossible or undoubtedly true. The argument follows a logical flow: establish urgency, then prioritize inquiry.

جواز
احتراز
محال

A) Because the prophet is always truthful

D) Because we must obey religious law

Key Takeaway
The rational precaution we apply to worldly dangers obligates us to investigate prophetic claims, because the afterlife is certain and the prophet's message is at least possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You take great caution when someone warns you of a worldly danger, even if they might be lying. Why do you not apply the same caution to the prophet's warning about the afterlife? What does your inconsistency say about your true priorities?
?

Are you preparing with even half the urgency? If not, what is holding you back from investigating his message with all your effort?
?
The prophet's claim is at least possible, and death is certain. You will face that claim after death. Is your current level of investigation—or lack thereof—something you would defend before your Creator? What is one concrete step you will take today to move from negligence to active inquiry?
